          <span class="play-btn-large">
           <span class="mw-tmh-playtext">
            Play media
           </span>
          </span>
         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RFA_Argus_arriving_at_Greenwich,_24_June_2017.ogv" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         RFA
         <i>
          Argus
         </i>
         being towed to Greenwich in June 2017
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Cutty_Sark" title="Cutty Sark">
         Cutty Sark
        </a>
       </i>
       (a
       <a href="/wiki/Clipper" title="Clipper">
        clipper
       </a>
       ship) has been preserved in a dry dock by the river. A major fire in May 2007 destroyed a part of the ship, although much had already been removed for restoration. Nearby for many years was also displayed
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Gipsy_Moth_IV" title="Gipsy Moth IV">
         Gipsy Moth IV
        </a>
       </i>
       , the 54 feet (16.5 m) yacht sailed by Sir
       <a href="/wiki/Francis_Chichester" title="Francis Chichester">
        Francis Chichester
       </a>
       in his single-handed, 226-day
       <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">
        circumnavigation
       </a>
       of the globe during 1966–67. In 2004,
       <i>
        Gipsy Moth IV
       </i>
       was removed from Greenwich, and after restoration work completed a second circumnavigation in May 2007. On the riverside in front of the north-west corner of the Hospital is an obelisk erected in memory of
       <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">
        Arctic
       </a>
       explorer
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Ren%C3%A9_Bellot" title="Joseph René Bellot">
        Joseph René Bellot
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GreatRiverRace08.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/GreatRiverRace08.JPG/220px-GreatRiverRace08.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/GreatRiverRace08.JPG/330px-GreatRiverRace08.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/GreatRiverRace08.JPG/440px-GreatRiverRace08.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GreatRiverRace08.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Boats at Greenwich at the end of the Great River Race
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="3072" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg/220px-HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg/330px-HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg/440px-HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HMS_Defender_at_Greenwich.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Royal Navy
         <a href="/wiki/Type_45_destroyer" title="Type 45 destroyer">
          Type 45 destroyer
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/HMS_Defender_(D36)" title="HMS Defender (D36)">
          HMS
          <i>
           Defender
          </i>
         </a>
         moored on the riverfront at Greenwich in 2015
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Near the Cutty Sark site, a circular building contains the entrance to the
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_foot_tunnel" title="Greenwich foot tunnel">
        Greenwich foot tunnel
       </a>
       , opened on 4 August 1902. This connects Greenwich to the
       <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Dogs" title="Isle of Dogs">
        Isle of Dogs
       </a>
       on the northern side of the River Thames. The north exit of the tunnel is at
       <a href="/wiki/Island_Gardens" title="Island Gardens">
        Island Gardens
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       from where the famous view of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenwich_Hospital_(London)" title="Greenwich Hospital (London)">
        Greenwich Hospital
       </a>
       painted by
       <a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">
        Canaletto
       </a>
       can be seen.
      </p>
      <p>
       Rowing has been part of life on the river at Greenwich for hundreds of years and the first Greenwich Regatta was held in 1785. The annual
       <a href="/wiki/Great_River_Race" title="Great River Race">
        Great River Race
       </a>
       along the Thames
       <a href="/wiki/Tideway" title="Tideway">
        Tideway
       </a>
       finishes at the Cutty Sark. The nearby Trafalgar Rowing Centre in Crane Street is home to
       <a href="/wiki/Curlew_Rowing_Club" title="Curlew Rowing Club">
        Curlew Rowing Club
       </a>
       and Globe Rowing Club.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Naval_College,_Greenwich" title="Royal Naval College, Greenwich">
        Old Royal Naval College
       </a>
       is Sir
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">
        Christopher Wren
       </a>
       's domed masterpiece at the centre of the heritage site. The site is administered by the Greenwich Foundation and several of the buildings are let to the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Greenwich" title="University of Greenwich">
        University of Greenwich
       </a>
       and one, the King Charles block, to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinity_College_of_Music" title="Trinity College of Music">
        Trinity College of Music
       </a>
       . Within the complex is the former college dining room, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Painted_Hall" title="Painted Hall">
        Painted Hall
       </a>
       , this was painted by
       <a href="/wiki/James_Thornhill" title="James Thornhill">
        James Thornhill
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Chapel,_Greenwich" title="St Paul's Chapel, Greenwich">
        Chapel of St Peter and St Paul
       </a>
       , with an interior designed by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_%27Athenian%27_Stuart" title="James 'Athenian' Stuart">
        James 'Athenian' Stuart
       </a>
       . The Naval College had a training reactor, the
       <a href="/wiki/JASON_reactor" title="JASON reactor">
        JASON reactor
       </a>
       , within the King William building that was operational between 1962 and 1996. The reactor was decommissioned and removed in 1999.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital,_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="480" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital%2C_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg/170px-Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital%2C_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital%2C_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg/255px-Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital%2C_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital%2C_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg/340px-Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital%2C_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Riverside_entrance_to_Trinity_Hospital,_Greenwich_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1164174.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Trinity Hospital, Greenwich
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       To the east of the Naval College is the
       <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Hospital,_Greenwich" title="Trinity Hospital, Greenwich">
        Trinity Hospital
       </a>
       almshouse, founded in 1613, the oldest surviving building in the town centre.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is next to the massive brick walls and the landing stage of
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Power_Station" title="Greenwich Power Station">
        Greenwich Power Station
       </a>
       . Built between 1902 and 1910 as a coal-fired station to supply power to
       <a href="/wiki/London_County_Council_Tramways" title="London County Council Tramways">
        London's tram system
       </a>
       , and later the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_underground" title="London underground">
        London underground
       </a>
       , it is now oil- and gas-powered and serves as a backup station for London Underground.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       East Greenwich also has a small park,
       <a href="/wiki/East_Greenwich_Pleasaunce" title="East Greenwich Pleasaunce">
        East Greenwich Pleasaunce
       </a>
       , which was formerly the burial ground of Greenwich Hospital.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_O2_(London)" title="The O2 (London)">
        The O
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
       </a>
       (formerly the
       <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Dome" title="Millennium Dome">
        Millennium Dome
       </a>
       ) was built on part of the site of
       <a href="/wiki/East_Greenwich_Gas_Works" title="East Greenwich Gas Works">
        East Greenwich Gas Works
       </a>
       , a disused
       <a href="/wiki/British_Gas_plc" title="British Gas plc">
        British Gas
       </a>
       site on the
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Peninsula" title="Greenwich Peninsula">
        Greenwich Peninsula
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is next to
       <a href="/wiki/North_Greenwich_tube_station" title="North Greenwich tube station">
        North Greenwich tube station
       </a>
       , about 3 miles (4.8 km) east from the Greenwich town centre, North West of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlton,_Greenwich" title="Charlton, Greenwich">
        Charlton
       </a>
       . Pear Tree Wharf was associated with the gas works, being used to unload coal for the manufacturing of town gas, and is now home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Yacht_Club" title="Greenwich Yacht Club">
        Greenwich Yacht Club
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Millennium_Village" title="Greenwich Millennium Village">
        Greenwich Millennium Village
       </a>
       is a new
       <a href="/wiki/Urban_renewal" title="Urban renewal">
        urban regeneration
       </a>
       development to the south of the Dome.
       <a href="/wiki/Enderby%27s_Wharf" title="Enderby's Wharf">
        Enderby's Wharf
       </a>
       is a site associated with
       <a href="/wiki/Submarine_communications_cable" title="Submarine communications cable">
        submarine cable
       </a>
       manufacture for over 150 years.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Greenwich_Park">
        Greenwich Park
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Greenwich Park">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Park" title="Greenwich Park">
        Greenwich Park
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Behind the former Naval College is the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Maritime_Museum" title="National Maritime Museum">
        National Maritime Museum
       </a>
       housed in buildings forming another symmetrical group and grand arcade around the
       <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_House" title="Queen's House">
        Queen's House
       </a>
       , designed by
       <a href="/wiki/Inigo_Jones" title="Inigo Jones">
        Inigo Jones
       </a>
       . Continuing to the south,
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Park" title="Greenwich Park">
        Greenwich Park
       </a>
       is a
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Parks_of_London" title="Royal Parks of London">
        Royal Park
       </a>
       of 183 acres (0.7 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ), laid out in the 17th century and formed from the hunting grounds of the Royal
       <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Placentia" title="Palace of Placentia">
        Palace of Placentia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg/220px-TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg/330px-TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg/440px-TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TulipStair_QueensHouse_Greenwich.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Spiral staircase and lantern at the
         <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_House" title="Queen's House">
          Queen's House
         </a>
         in Greenwich
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The park rises towards
       <a href="/wiki/Blackheath,_London" title="Blackheath, London">
        Blackheath
       </a>
       and at the top of this hill is a statue of
       <a href="/wiki/James_Wolfe" title="James Wolfe">
        James Wolfe
       </a>
       , commander of the British expedition to capture
       <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">
        Quebec
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nearby a major group of buildings within the park includes the former
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Observatory,_Greenwich" title="Royal Observatory, Greenwich">
        Royal Observatory, Greenwich
       </a>
       ; the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Meridian" title="Prime Meridian">
        Prime Meridian
       </a>
       passes through this building.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">
        Greenwich Mean Time
       </a>
       was at one time based on the time observations made at the Royal Greenwich Observatory, before being superseded by
       <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
        Coordinated Universal Time
       </a>
       . While there is no longer a working astronomical observatory at Greenwich, a
       <a href="/wiki/Time_ball" title="Time ball">
        ball
       </a>
       still drops daily to mark the exact moment of 1 p.m., and there is a museum of astronomical and navigational tools, particularly
       <a href="/wiki/John_Harrison" title="John Harrison">
        John Harrison
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Marine_chronometer" title="Marine chronometer">
        marine chronometers
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Ranger%27s_House" title="Ranger's House">
        Ranger's House
       </a>
       lies at the Blackheath end of the park and houses the Wernher Collection of art,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and many fine houses, including
       <a href="/wiki/John_Vanbrugh" title="John Vanbrugh">
        Vanbrugh's house
       </a>
       lie on Maze Hill, on the western edge of the park.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Town_centre">
        Town centre
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Town centre">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Greenwich,_England_2.jpg">
         <img alt="A curving street with older two- and three-storey buildings on either side. In front is a black London taxicab with an advert; midway down the street is an intersection with heavy traffic. A cupolaed clock tower rises in the rear" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3966" data-file-width="5874" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Downtown_Greenwich%2C_England_2.jpg/220px-Downtown_Greenwich%2C_England_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Downtown_Greenwich%2C_England_2.jpg/330px-Downtown_Greenwich%2C_England_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Downtown_Greenwich%2C_England_2.jpg/440px-Downtown_Greenwich%2C_England_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Greenwich,_England_2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Town centre
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Georgian and Victorian architecture dominates in the town centre which spreads to the west of the park and Royal Naval College. Much of this forms a one-way system around a covered market,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenwich_Market" title="Greenwich Market">
        Greenwich Market
       </a>
       and the arthouse Greenwich Cinema. Up the hill from the centre, there are many streets of Georgian houses, including the
       <a href="/wiki/Fan_Museum" title="Fan Museum">
        Fan Museum
       </a>
       , on Croom's Hill. Nearby at the junction of Croom's Hill with Nevada Street, is
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Theatre" title="Greenwich Theatre">
        Greenwich Theatre
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Playhouse" title="Greenwich Playhouse">
        Greenwich Playhouse
       </a>
       closed in 2012
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Market">
        Market
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Market">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg">
         <img alt="An interior of a building with a translucent glass roof supported by blue-painted steel latticework. On the main floor are a number of different stalls with customers inspecting various wares." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4032" data-file-width="6048" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg/220px-Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg/330px-Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg/440px-Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenwich_Market_interior.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Greenwich Market
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There has been a market at Greenwich since the 14th century, but the history of the present market dates from 1700 when a charter to run two markets, on Wednesdays and Saturdays, was assigned by Lord Romney (
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Sydney,_1st_Earl_of_Romney" title="Henry Sydney, 1st Earl of Romney">
        Henry, Earl of Romney
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Green_17-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Green-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) to the Commissioners of Greenwich Hospital for 1000 years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The market is part of "the Island site", bounded by College Approach, Greenwich Church Street, King William Walk and Nelson Road, near the National Maritime Museum and the Royal Observatory. The buildings surrounding the market are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grade_2_listed" title="Grade 2 listed">
        Grade 2 listed
       </a>
       and were established in 1827–1833 under the direction of
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kay_(architect)" title="Joseph Kay (architect)">
        Joseph Kay
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heritage_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Heritage-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phantom_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Phantom-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A market roof was added in 1902–08 (and replaced in 2016). Later significant development occurred in 1958–60 and during the 1980s. The landowner, Greenwich Hospital, has been enhancing the Market since 2014 and due to complete in Spring 2016.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Greenwich_Mean_Time">
        Greenwich Mean Time
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Greenwich Mean Time">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">
        Greenwich Mean Time
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg/220px-Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg/330px-Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg/440px-Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenwich-Royal_Observatory-016.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Royal Observatory with the
         <a href="/wiki/Time_ball" title="Time ball">
          time ball
         </a>
         atop the Octagon Room
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Greenwich Mean Time (GMT) is a term originally referring to
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_time" title="Solar time">
        mean solar time
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Observatory,_Greenwich" title="Royal Observatory, Greenwich">
        Royal Observatory, Greenwich
       </a>
       in Greenwich. It is commonly used in practice to refer to
       <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
        Coordinated Universal Time
       </a>
       (UTC) when this is viewed as a
       <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">
        time zone
       </a>
       , especially by bodies connected with the United Kingdom, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">
        BBC World Service
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
        Royal Navy
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">
        Met Office
       </a>
       and others, although strictly UTC is an
       <a href="/wiki/Atomic_clock" title="Atomic clock">
        atomic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Time_standard" title="Time standard">
        time scale
       </a>
       which only approximates GMT with a tolerance of 0.9 second. It is also used to refer to
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_Time" title="Universal Time">
        Universal Time
       </a>
       (UT), which is a standard astronomical concept used in many technical fields and is referred to by the phrase
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zulu_time" title="Zulu time">
        Zulu time
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As the United Kingdom grew into an advanced
       <a href="/wiki/Maritime_nation" title="Maritime nation">
        maritime nation
       </a>
       , British mariners kept at least one
       <a href="/wiki/Marine_chronometer" title="Marine chronometer">
        chronometer
       </a>
       on GMT in order to calculate their
       <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">
        longitude
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_meridian" title="Prime meridian">
        Greenwich meridian
       </a>
       , which was by convention considered to have longitude zero degrees (this convention was internationally adopted in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Meridian_Conference" title="International Meridian Conference">
        International Meridian Conference
       </a>
       of 1884).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [note 1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Note that the synchronization of the
       <a href="/wiki/Marine_chronometer" title="Marine chronometer">
        chronometer
       </a>
       on GMT did not affect shipboard time itself, which was still solar time. But this practice, combined with mariners from other nations drawing from
       <a href="/wiki/Nevil_Maskelyne" title="Nevil Maskelyne">
        Nevil Maskelyne
       </a>
       's method of
       <a href="/wiki/Lunar_distance_(navigation)" title="Lunar distance (navigation)">
        lunar distances
       </a>
       based on observations at Greenwich, eventually led to GMT being used worldwide as a reference time independent of location. Most time zones were based upon this reference as a number of hours and half-hours "ahead of GMT" or "behind GMT".
      </p>
      <p>
       In recognition of the suburb's astronomical links,
       <a href="/wiki/2830_Greenwich" title="2830 Greenwich">
        Asteroid 2830
       </a>
       has been named 'Greenwich'.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_heritage_site">
        World heritage site
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: World heritage site">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em">
       <caption class="category">
        Maritime Greenwich
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th class="fn org" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;padding:0.2em;background:#ddd;">
         <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
          UNESCO World Heritage Site
         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top:1px #aaa solid;padding-top:0.4em;">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Naval_College_2008.jpg">
          <img alt="Royal Naval College 2008.jpg" data-file-height="1215" data-file-width="1800" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Royal_Naval_College_2008.jpg/220px-Royal_Naval_College_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Royal_Naval_College_2008.jpg/330px-Royal_Naval_College_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Royal_Naval_College_2008.jpg/440px-Royal_Naval_College_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
         </a>
         <div>
          Old Royal Naval College and University of Greenwich buildings on the bank of the River Thames
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color: #e7dcc3;">
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.3em;">
         <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site#Selection_criteria" title="World Heritage Site">
          Criteria
         </a>
        </th>
        <td class="category">
         Cultural: i, ii, iv, vi
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.3em;">
         Reference
        </th>
        <td>
         <a class="external text" href="http://whc.unesco.org/en/list/795" rel="nofollow">
          795
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.3em;">
         Inscription
        </th>
        <td>
         1997
         <small>
          (21st
          <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Committee" title="World Heritage Committee">
           Session
          </a>
          )
         </small>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.3em;">
         Area
        </th>
        <td class="category">
         109.5 ha
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

         Buffer zone
        </th>

         174.85 ha
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In 1997, Maritime Greenwich was added to the list of
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Sites
       </a>
       , for the concentration and quality of buildings of historic and architectural interest. These can be divided into the group of buildings along the riverfront,
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Park" title="Greenwich Park">
        Greenwich Park
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Georgian_era" title="Georgian era">
        Georgian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">
        Victorian
       </a>
       town centre.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Greenwich_Heritage_Centre">
        Greenwich Heritage Centre
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Greenwich Heritage Centre">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Heritage_Centre" title="Greenwich Heritage Centre">
        Greenwich Heritage Centre
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Greenwich Heritage Centre is a
       <a href="/wiki/Museum" title="Museum">
        museum
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Local_history" title="Local history">
        local history
       </a>
       resource run by the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Borough_of_Greenwich" title="Royal Borough of Greenwich">
        Royal Borough of Greenwich
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and is based in Artillery Square, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Arsenal" title="Royal Arsenal">
        Royal Arsenal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Woolwich" title="Woolwich">
        Woolwich
       </a>
       , south-east London.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Discover_Greenwich_Visitor_Centre">
        Discover Greenwich Visitor Centre
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Discover Greenwich Visitor Centre">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="4839" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg/220px-Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg/330px-Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg/440px-Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Samuel_pepys_building_greenwich.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Pepys Building
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        Discover Greenwich Visitor Centre
       </b>
       provides an introduction to the history and attractions in the Greenwich
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Site
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is located in the Pepys Building near to the
       <a href="/wiki/Cutty_Sark" title="Cutty Sark">
        Cutty Sark
       </a>
       within the grounds of the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Royal_Naval_College" title="Old Royal Naval College">
        Old Royal Naval College
       </a>
       (formerly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenwich_Hospital_(London)" title="Greenwich Hospital (London)">
        Greenwich Hospital
       </a>
       ); the building began life as an engineering laboratory for the College. The centre opened in March 2010, and admission is free.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Centre explains the history of Greenwich as a royal residence and a maritime centre. Exhibits include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        The history of the
        <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Placentia" title="Palace of Placentia">
         Palace of Placentia
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Models of
        <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">
         Christopher Wren
        </a>
        's original designs for
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenwich_Hospital_(London)" title="Greenwich Hospital (London)">
         Greenwich Hospital
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Six of the carved heads originally intended to decorate the exterior of the College's
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Painted_Hall" title="Painted Hall">
         Painted Hall
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Exhibition displays about Maritime Greenwich and its connections with the sea and exploration.
       </li>
       <li>
        <i>
         "By Wisdom as much as War"
        </i>
        – an exhibition about the history of the
        <a href="/wiki/Old_Royal_Naval_College" title="Old Royal Naval College">
         Royal Naval College
        </a>
        during the years it occupied Greenwich Hospital (1873–1998).
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Greenwich" title="List of schools in Greenwich">
        List of schools in Greenwich
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Greenwich" title="University of Greenwich">
        University of Greenwich
       </a>
       main campus is located in the distinctive buildings of the former
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Royal_Naval_College" title="Old Royal Naval College">
        Royal Naval College
       </a>
       . The university has other campuses at Avery Hill in
       <a href="/wiki/Eltham" title="Eltham">
        Eltham
       </a>
       and at
       <a href="/wiki/Medway" title="Medway">
        Medway
       </a>
       . The Greenwich campus also houses the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trinity_College_of_Music" title="Trinity College of Music">
        Trinity College of Music
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Secondary schools in the area include
       <a href="/wiki/John_Roan_School" title="John Roan School">
        John Roan School
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/St_Ursula%27s_Convent_School" title="St Ursula's Convent School">
        St Ursula's Convent School
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">
        Transport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenwich_railway_station_(crop).JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1350" data-file-width="2698" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Greenwich_railway_station_%28crop%29.JPG/220px-Greenwich_railway_station_%28crop%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Greenwich_railway_station_%28crop%29.JPG/330px-Greenwich_railway_station_%28crop%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Greenwich_railway_station_%28crop%29.JPG/440px-Greenwich_railway_station_%28crop%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenwich_railway_station_(crop).JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_station" title="Greenwich station">
          Greenwich station
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">
        Rail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Rail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Greenwich is served by two
       <a href="/wiki/National_Rail" title="National Rail">
        National Rail
       </a>
       stations,
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_station" title="Greenwich station">
        Greenwich
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maze_Hill_station" title="Maze Hill station">
        Maze Hill
       </a>
       . Both of these stations have services to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Charing_Cross" title="London Charing Cross">
        London Charing Cross
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/London_Cannon_Street" title="London Cannon Street">
        London Cannon Street
       </a>
       , London Cannon Street via
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bexleyheath_station" title="Bexleyheath station">
        Bexleyheath
       </a>
       , London Cannon Street via
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sidcup_station" title="Sidcup station">
        Sidcup
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dartford_station" title="Dartford station">
        Dartford
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gillingham_(Kent)_railway_station" title="Gillingham (Kent) railway station">
        Gillingham
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Greenwich is also served by the
       <a href="/wiki/Docklands_Light_Railway" title="Docklands Light Railway">
        Docklands Light Railway
       </a>
       , with services from Greenwich and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cutty_Sark_station" title="Cutty Sark station">
        Cutty Sark
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Lewisham_station" title="Lewisham station">
        Lewisham
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf_DLR_station" title="Canary Wharf DLR station">
        Canary Wharf
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Stratford_station" title="Stratford station">
        Stratford
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank%E2%80%93Monument_station" title="Bank–Monument station">
        Bank
       </a>
       . Greenwich is also served by
       <a href="/wiki/North_Greenwich_tube_station" title="North Greenwich tube station">
        North Greenwich tube station
       </a>
       which is on the northern tip of the district as well as the whole surrounding borough. The station is on the
       <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_line" title="Jubilee line">
        Jubilee line
       </a>
       and has westward services through central London to Stanmore, and eastward services to Stratford.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Buses">
        Buses
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Buses">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Greenwich is served by several
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_London" title="Transport for London">
        Transport for London
       </a>
       bus services which links it with areas including
       <a href="/wiki/Catford" title="Catford">
        Catford
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Central_London" title="Central London">
        Central London
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Elephant_and_Castle" title="Elephant and Castle">
        Elephant and Castle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eltham" title="Eltham">
        Eltham
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lewisham" title="Lewisham">
        Lewisham
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peckham" title="Peckham">
        Peckham
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/New_Cross" title="New Cross">
        New Cross
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sidcup" title="Sidcup">
        Sidcup
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Thamesmead" title="Thamesmead">
        Thamesmead
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Waterloo,_London" title="Waterloo, London">
        Waterloo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Woolwich" title="Woolwich">
        Woolwich
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Boat">
        Boat
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Boat">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       There are a number of river boat services running from
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Pier" title="Greenwich Pier">
        Greenwich Pier
       </a>
       , managed by
       <a href="/wiki/London_River_Services" title="London River Services">
        London River Services
       </a>
       . The main services include the Thames commuter catamaran service run by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thames_Clipper" title="Thames Clipper">
        Thames Clipper
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Embankment_Pier" title="Embankment Pier">
        Embankment
       </a>
       , via
       <a href="/wiki/Tower_Millennium_Pier" title="Tower Millennium Pier">
        Tower Millennium Pier
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Wharf_Pier" title="Canary Wharf Pier">
        Canary Wharf
       </a>
       and on to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_O2_(London)" title="The O2 (London)">
        O
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Woolwich_Arsenal_Pier" title="Woolwich Arsenal Pier">
        Woolwich Arsenal Pier
       </a>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Millennium_Pier" title="Westminster Millennium Pier">
        Westminster
       </a>
       -Greenwich cruise service by
       <a href="/wiki/Thames_River_Services" title="Thames River Services">
        Thames River Services
       </a>
       ; and the
       <a href="/wiki/City_Cruises" title="City Cruises">
        City Cruises
       </a>
       tourist cruise via Westminster,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waterloo_Millennium_Pier" title="Waterloo Millennium Pier">
        Waterloo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tower_Millennium_Pier" title="Tower Millennium Pier">
        Tower
       </a>
       piers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pedestrian_and_cycle_routes">
        Pedestrian and cycle routes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Pedestrian and cycle routes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Thames_Path" title="Thames Path">
        Thames Path
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Trail" title="National Trail">
        National Trail
       </a>
       runs along the riverside.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_foot_tunnel" title="Greenwich foot tunnel">
        Greenwich foot tunnel
       </a>
       provides pedestrian access to the southern end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Dogs" title="Isle of Dogs">
        Isle of Dogs
       </a>
       , across the river Thames.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/National_Cycle_Network" title="National Cycle Network">
        National Cycle Network
       </a>
       Route 1 includes the foot tunnel, though cycling is not permitted in the tunnel itself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Greenwich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_Lear" title="Edward Lear">
        Edward Lear
       </a>
       makes reference to Greenwich in
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=More_Nonsense_Pictures,_Rhymes,_Botany,_etc&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="More Nonsense Pictures, Rhymes, Botany, etc (page does not exist)">
         More Nonsense Pictures, Rhymes, Botany, etc
        </a>
       </i>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <br/>
      </p>
      <p>
       There was a young lady of Greenwich,
       <br/>
       Whose garments were bordered with Spinach;
       <br/>
       But a large spotty calf
       <br/>
       Bit her shawl quite in half,
       <br/>
       Which alarmed that young lady of Greenwich.
      </p>
